<text>This facility is not secured overnight. The pedestrian gates and doors to the buildings are left completely unlocked and in some cases left propped open. If they have an alarm system they don't set it.

I had a stack of boxes fall on me in one of their units. Totally my fault. But I was hurt pretty bad and I thought I should go to urgent care for the pain in my back and ankle. By the time I crammed the stuff back in my storage unit and hobbled to my vehicle, it was a few minutes after their 7:00pm closing time. When I entered my code to the vehicle exit gate it said "access denied, no after hours access." I found an employee named Diego who tried his gate code and got the same result. Diego said he would go to the office and get a gate code that would work. He never came back.

By 7:45 I had called every phone number I had for All Right Storage and sent them an email. I even called their facility in Irvine hoping to catch someone by luck. I decided to try to track down Diego or any other employee. For almost 2 hours I wandered that facility yelling and making noise. Walking in and out of buildings, through gates, opening closed doors, etc and no one ever approached me. I never set off an alarm. I never encountered a single employee or security patrol. Needless to say if I had been a thief, no one would have stopped me from popping every lock in that place. A thief couldn't get his car on property, but that's no problem since even their dolly and cart area was unsecured and all the pedestrian gates to the street were wide open. I eventually found a friend to pick me up and I had to return for my car the next day.

I spoke to the facility manager. Basically, his response was that I shouldn't have been there after 7 and it's normal for the entire facility to be left unsecured overnight. Because "in 8 years we've never had a problem." He said that to the guy with the problem, unbelievable, right?< /text><resp>None</resp>< Date>

1508566427881< /Date>
<rate>2<//rate>< review>
If you've never been to Steak 'n Shake outside of California then you will never know how good it really is.

Living in Florida, I always sit at the counter right where I can see them cook my burger fresh - with all the grease and all heat from the grill I watch my meal being cooked and prepared. Although I am thankful to the franchisees for bringing this out to the West, it is still a far distance from how it's really done and how it really tastes.

The burgers here at the Daly City location were dry as if they were reheated. The fries were cold and chalky. The shakes tasted like they came from a machine and not hand scooped and manually placed  in a mixer by servers as they do in the South. They didn't even have pepper sauce. When I asked the server he came back with black pepper. The only consistent thing that they offer here are the paperboard cars.

The service was horrible, checkout was long as they didn't seem to know how to use the Steak 'n Shake app.

Not a good experience and it just made me miss the real Steak 'n Shakes back in Florida along with that hometown Southern Hospitality.</review>

<Review>In two words, don't bother.

I drive past this location every morning, and I have been eagerly anticipating the opening for weeks.  I didn't check the reviews before I visited so I could keep an open mind.  I had heard from friends that they waited in line for up to two hours before they seated.  That seemed reasonable for a new restaurant, but I soon discovered that the wait time was not because Steak 'n Shake had reached capacity.

We arrived at 2 pm on Friday.  Our arrival time was the best part of our visit because their milkshakes are 50% off on weekdays from 2 to 5 p.m.  The milkshakes are good, they have a large variety, and the price is reasonable at 50%.

On the other hand, they do not think of themselves as a fast-food joint even though the food is fast-food quality.  This means you cannot walk up to the counter and order takeout.  We watched multiple people park, enter the business, and try to order food, only to be rebuffed by the staff.

These people didn't know how lucky they were.  The primary problem with Steak 'n Shake is that it takes too long to get your food and the staff is low quality.  I noticed during the weeks leading to the launch date that they were willing to hire anyone without any experience and it shows in the front staff and the back.  After we had been seated, it took the waitress twenty minutes to take our order, and she had difficulty writing it down.  When you order a burger, you have several options for toppings (tomatoes, onions, lettuce, mayonnaise, ketchup, and mustard).  The waitress wrote everything out longhand on a piece of paper instead of having a bunch of checkboxes.  Writing out an order takes longer and is hard for the kitchen staff to read.

Our food took over thirty minutes to arrive, and this is a common complaint - food takes too long to come and is cold when it gets to your table.  I was so amazed that I went to the kitchen area to observe the staff preparing the food.  There are a lot of people in the back, but the setup is inefficient compared to other burger places.  Two people are assigned to the grill and apparently spend their time trying to decipher the orders and figure out how many burgers and patties to cook.  Once the meat is ready, they assemble the burger and put it under a warmer.  At this point, another duo takes over and puts on the correct toppings.  Somehow this process takes forever, and the take-out queue is mixed in with the sit-down customers.

There are no napkins on any of the tables, and our table did not have ketchup.

Our food came before our milkshakes.  The burgers and the fries were both cold because they had been under a warmer for a long time.  Our order had two mistakes in it.  First, my wife ordered a burger with two patties but only received one patty.  When we brought this up with our waitress, she said the patties were thin, and there might be two in there.  We had to open up the hamburger before she admitted there had been a mistake.  She said it would take another thirty minutes to prepare the correct burger.  I asked if we could get our bill adjusted instead, and she replied that she would have to take it to her manager.

The second mistake was that my wife ordered a raspberry milkshake, but it did not come to our table.  Our waitress had forgotten to put it on the bill.  Fortunately, she found the drink in the kitchen.

The fries are thin, cold, and hard.

At this point, I began checking the reviews and realized our experience was not atypical.

The final insult came when I tried to pay for the bill at the counter.  The bill had increased from the first time I saw it.  The waitress added the shake to our bill but neglected to adjust it for the missing patty.  I had to explain everything to her again because she had completely forgotten the original complaint.

Tried once, never going back, don't waste your time.< /Review><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>
None</resp>

<review>01/04/2017 at 3pm update: I was pleasantly surprised giving this place a second chance.  You can read my first review below.  Drove right up to the speaker and ordered,  to the first window to pay,  and about 60 seconds for the car in front of me to get their food,  drove up to the second window and was immediately handed my food.  3 minutes tops and i was back on the road.  MUCH better than over an hour for 10 cars. If this is the knew norm,  i strongly recommend giving them a chance.  I haven't checked if they allow you to order to go yet.  But at least the drive -thru was a breeze.
Not Happy.  Food's decent. I prefer thicker fries. But they do not do to-go orders at the counter.  Dine-in or Drive-thru only.  Inconvenient when you're driving a dually truck weighing 11,000lbs. Well, let's go get stuck in the narrow drive-thru driveway and scratch my Alcoas. I would strongly suggest a walk-up window or to-go option so those of us who work AND drive for a living don't get stuck in the horrible drive-thru line.  20 cars took over an hour last time. And it's bloody stupid because the drive-thru line blocks anyone trying to park in their lot.  NO THOUGHT went into the parking lot. Don't worry about being able to find a parking spot because there are plenty available even at the busiest hour.  The problem is unless you're on a motorcycle or bicycle or walking,  you'll never make it to the spot.  And I've moved 2 car lengths in over 10 minutes.
Update,  3 car lengths in 20 minutes.  There goes my lunch.  I don't know about dine-in, but avoid the drive-thru unless you have AT LEAST 1/4 tank of fuel and feel like cross the bay bridge during rush hour. I was treated by Dr. Villar. I came in for a cracked molar that had turned into a deep cavity. When we spoke he made it clear that you have to try and do everything you can to save the tooth first and a root canal should always be a last resort. After seeing the x-rays and cold testing my tooth we came up with a treatment plan for me to get a distil wedge and a deep filling in an effort to save my tooth before we try anything else. He made it clear the entire time that he wanted to give my tooth a fighting chance. I came in the next day and was feeling a little anxious since this was my first filling in like 20 years, but he made sure I was comfortable and ready for the procedure. < review>
I first came in to see you in July, 2003 with a small 4 week orange male tabby (Bailey) that my son brought over to my condo with his eye totally infected.  He found this kitten in a dumpster.  You took care of him, giving him the proper shots and eye medication and antibiotics and informed me after a few visits that he would be blind in his one eye and it would eventually have to be removed.  You were his vet until two years later when I moved to Dana Point.  However, when Bailey seemed to have an ear infection I took him to another vet in Laguna Beach (Dr. Susan Davis - BIG MISTAKE) instead of taking him to Dr. Craft (who you recommended)-  her associate vet gave him an antibiotic shot along with a booster shot at the same time. Costing me $$$$.   One day later he would not eat, would not drink, did not use his litter box and was hiding and acting spastic - ‚Äì long story short took him to an emergency veterinarian hospital in Mission Viejo at 10 pm where they re-hydrated him with IV fluids because he had a fever exceeding 108 and kept him overnight for $900.  I picked him up the next morning (Friday) and returned to the vet in Laguna Beach where she said she couldn't help him and referred me to a "specialist" that would charge $1200 to walk in the door.  I called you at 4:45 pm that day and you said to bring in Bailey and you would wait for him ‚Äì because of traffic I didn't arrive at your office until after 6 pm on a Friday night.  You knew exactly what was wrong with him, stating giving a booster shot AND an antibiotic shot at the same time should never be done.  You gave him a cortisone shot and told me to bring him back in the morning.  He was 50% better that night and by the next day was 90% better and by the end of the week was doing just fine.  Since that time I recommended you to all my friends at church, at work and all my family.  I wish I could find another vet like you here in Arizona ‚Äì they just don't meet up to my standards because of you.  Bailey is now 12 and an indoor car living in a wonderful home and healthy!

< userid>
111644673136196029337< /userid>
<Time>1621638364404<//Time>< review>
The intimate, Philippe Stack designed, Katsuya Hollywood is complex, expensive, and brilliantly eclectic.  The Sushi Chefs bring the confident skill that compliments the modern artistic environment. Their sashimi plate is gorgeous.

The large reception area is decorated in a geometric pattern of twelve, three foot (1m) tall, twelve inchs (30 cm) square solid, under-lit, clear plastic resin columns, embedded with white knives. It is a homage to the tool of the sushi chef.

Shannon, our hostess, led us to one of two dinning rooms. The dining area, hidden behind a curtain.  Parting the curtain you enter a darkened dining room, that has just enough soft lighting for a romantic effect. The large wall facing us is covered with a giant photo of a brightly lit, seductive woman's eyes. She is always watching.

Katsuya was awarded "Travel and Leisure's" award for best design. The chairs are oversized and well padded. The tables are large enough to be comfortable. As the room fills it can be difficult to hear your companion.

Yes, Katsuya is wheelchair accessible. However it not easy. Here's how it's done. First, one of your party steps up the entrance stairway and let's the reception desk know a guest in a wheelchair ( or handicap) requires access. You and the disabled guest travel North to Hollywood Boulevard, turn West (left) and move past the "Pie Hole Restaurant" to a small unmarked door. Here you will be greated and taken into Katsuya. It is worth the effort.

Kyle, our server, is knowledgeable and friendly. We were presented with two menus, conventional and vegan. The conventional menu is extensive. The
vegan menu is two-thirds shorter. We ordered from the vegan menu.

Our meal, consisting of vegan appetizers: vegetable sushi, crispy rice and avocado, and crispy, shaved brussel sprouts. Each was prepared with care and artistry. Katsuya has four kitchens.

Parking is difficult and expensive.</review>

<username>Albert K< /username><Date>1523513095021<//Date>< rate>
4<//rate>
< Review>
Took a large party to Katsuya. The food is very delicious - especially the super soft steak, the seaweed salad, and the salmon. The drinks are well created also. The whole meal inclusive for 8 people was about $750, so you should expect to spend $70-$90/head.

One issue with the venue was the understaffing. The food came out very quickly and sporadically; however, there was one lady taking care of half the restaurant. It's not her fault at all, but she was assigned to 10+ tables, which included 50+ people. As a result, you get your drinks slowly, refills slower, and the experience is shot.

For over $100 gratuity, I'd expect a bit faster service. Again, this is no fault of the waitress as she hauled ass, but the restaurant needs to increase their staff, especially during dinner rushes prior to shows.

I'll go again at some point as I really like the food, but will refrain from hosting a client event here.< /Review>

< Text>
This is a great pre-Pantages show dinner, drinks, snacks option. No need to get a table (unless you want to) the bar has full service and a great happy hour (at the bar 5pm - 7pm).

The happy hour menu may be small but there is a solid variety: rolls, nigiri, cocktails, and small plates. Everything is under $10 so if you have a small group you can have a great meal/snack for only part of the cost.

Since it is literally down the street from the Pantages Theatre it is a perfect pre-show option.

They do have valet for $14 and they will let you leave your car with valet while you enjoy a Pantages show!< /Text>

<Text>Had an amazing Sunday night at Katsuya! My second time at the chain, but first at that location. I stuck with some of my choices from my first katsuya experience, but branched out as well. The Miso Glazed Black Cod was amazing, as usual; My favorite meal whenever it's offered on a menu.  The baked crab hand roll was tender and delicious as well! For our new choices, the truffle ponzu ceviche had amazing flavor and a plethora of fish choices. Finally, we went with the rock shrimp tempura roll. A lot of tasty shrimp on top for perfection! It was the perfect amount of spicy for a non-spicy lover like myself.
Service was also good! Always attended to.

All in all, I would definitely make a trip to katsuya. And if you have the budget splurge on the hot and cold courses. The rolls are delicious, but you can get specialty rolls at almost Japanese sushi places!</Text><userid>111510771506868899617< /userid></record>

<Text>Amazing! Came for an early dinner after a matinee at Pantages, and was very impressed. We had a reservation and were seated right away. The servers were very attentive and explained everything we asked about. The decor was very interesting and elegant. We felt cool just being there, haha. We started with the gyoza, which were perfect. I had the famous miso black cod, which was LITERALLY melt-in-your-mouth tender. Like, I had never tasted fish like that, it was spectacular. My wife, who doesn't like seafood at all, had the teriyaki chicken, which she said was the best she had ever had. The bad:  Staff was horrible, table was ready 25mins late for our reservation (even though the place was dead), server messed up our order many times and never came to our table to check on us, refill drinks, etc.

< userid>
110006480612793104456<//userid>
< user_name>
Steven Vong< /user_name>
<date>1430935812047< /date><rate>3</rate>< review>
This is one of those places where you only need to eat there once.

After all the hype (celebrity sightings) and hearing all of my friends talk about this place, my friend and I decided to eat here for DineLA week. We made reservations for Thursday night at 7:00 PM.

The location is cool near the middle of Hollywood, near the Pantages and other theatres, concealed in a corner of the Boulevard. There is no place to find cheap parking so we paid $10 for the valet (expensive).

The entrance of the restaurant looks pretty cool, it's all glass so you can see the bar and contemporary designed environment. There are a lot of homeless people near the stairs on the sidewalk though, which made it awkward waiting for the valet/ standing outside the restaurant.

The restaurant wasn't too busy (but it got busy later when only one big table was empty), music was playing loud and the bar was packed. We were both ready to order since we knew the menu but the waitress didn't take our order until 5 minutes later.

The appetizer came out a couple of minutes later. I had onion albacore, which was much more onion than albacore. It was flavorful, but tiny, which left me unsatisfied. My friend ordered crispy rice with spicy tuna which was really good. However, there were only two pieces so the portion was too tiny. Then again, it was DineLA price so I guess it was only a sample.

Anyways, a long time later we got our tonkatsu. The tray looked nice. The beef bits and mushroom were tender and delicious, though a little salty. The glaze made the whole dish really good.

Last we got ice cream mochi, a single piece cut in half with a few pieces of fruit and panna cotta. Nothing special.

In conclusion, the food was good (highlights being the crispy rice and beef) but nothing amazing, the environment was modern and mostly aesthetically pleasing, and the service was average (food took forever but the waiters actually refilled my water lol). The sushi was better than most, but for its price the experience was not worth it. Katsuya definitely doesn't live up to its hype and celebrities really need to get better taste if they keep coming here.

(Side note: The bathrooms are really cool but kinda creepy. The napkins are reallly really nice)< /review>
